  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_583bfee7-c764-4715-b67d-f2ea8fccdc10'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer7666766670103905568">Three years ago, Sophie Mercer discovered that she was a witch. It's gotten her into a few scrapes. Her non-gifted mother has been as supportive as possible, consulting Sophie's estranged father—an elusive European warlock—only when necessary. But when Sophie attracts too much human attention for a prom-night spell gone horribly wrong, it's her dad who decides her punishme</span>
  <span id="freeText7666766670103905568" style="display:none">Three years ago, Sophie Mercer discovered that she was a witch. It's gotten her into a few scrapes. Her non-gifted mother has been as supportive as possible, consulting Sophie's estranged father—an elusive European warlock—only when necessary. But when Sophie attracts too much human attention for a prom-night spell gone horribly wrong, it's her dad who decides her punishment: exile to Hex Hall, an isolated reform school for wayward Prodigium, a.k.a. witches, faeries, and shapeshifters. <p>By the end of her first day among fellow freak-teens, Sophie has quite a scorecard: three powerful enemies who look like supermodels, a futile crush on a gorgeous warlock, a creepy tag-along ghost, and a new roommate who happens to be the most hated person and only vampire student on campus. Worse, Sophie soon learns that a mysterious predator has been attacking students, and her only friend is the number-one suspect. </p><p>As a series of blood-curdling mysteries starts to converge, Sophie prepares for the biggest threat of all: an ancient secret society determined to destroy all Prodigium, especially her.</p></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_8416817').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_8416817').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_8416817').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_54683410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54683410" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54683410?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=own-arc">own-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54683410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9821280054136061118">I've wanted to be a witch forever. Long before anyone uttered the words Harry & Potter. You see, there was this awesome movie called Teen Witch. Have you seen it? Well the girl finds out she is witch, turns her little brother into a dog, gets to meet a famous singer AND snags the most popular boy at school. All because she had magical powers. I so wanted to be a witch.<br/><br/>Perhaps that is why I loved this book so much, or maybe it's because Hex Hall is a laugh-out-load, fast paced and easy read. It c</span>
  <span id="freeText9821280054136061118" style="display:none">I've wanted to be a witch forever. Long before anyone uttered the words Harry &amp; Potter. You see, there was this awesome movie called Teen Witch. Have you seen it? Well the girl finds out she is witch, turns her little brother into a dog, gets to meet a famous singer AND snags the most popular boy at school. All because she had magical powers. I so wanted to be a witch.<br /><br />Perhaps that is why I loved this book so much, or maybe it's because Hex Hall is a laugh-out-load, fast paced and easy read. It could really go either way. The point is, however, that it was marvelous.<br /><br />I've been trying to write this review for days. I'm not sure why I find it so difficult to explain why I find something so enjoyable, but for whatever the reason I do. Ask me why I don't like something, I can write you a list a mile long, but describe why I like it.... I just do that's why!<br /><br />It could be Sophie, the main character. She is just an enjoyable protagonist. She's caring, open-minded, a good friend, and she might be a little gullible at times, but that is what makes her so great. She isn't a perfect character, she makes mistakes and we get to laugh at her for it! Well sometimes.<br /><br />Maybe it was the plot. I will admit at times it was a little predictable, but it was never slow. And I might have thought I knew what was going on, but Hawkin's really threw me for a loop. I'm sure it will leave you craving the next novel as much as I am.<br /><br />Then again it was probably the writing. Simplistic and addicting.<br /><br />I might not be able to vividly express why I thought it was amazing, but it just was. I'm so very much looking forward to the next novel and more of Sophie's adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9821280054136061118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187038104" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187038104" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187038104?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187038104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2771295587564914710">OK, I originally gave this 3.5 stars.. but I have decided just to give it 4 stars. <br/><br/><i>“I’m experiencing some teenage angst, Mrs Casnoff,” I answered. “I need to, like, write it in my journal or something.”</i><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>Wow, I read that book in about five hours…. I probably should get some food. Laughter is the only sustenance I need.<br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/><u>Groundskeepers.</u><br/><br/>Sorry, what was the question? <br/>Sophie. Jenna. Boarding school. MAGICAL BOARDING SCHOOL FOR DELINQUENT PARANORMALS. Ghosts. Flirt</span>
  <span id="freeText2771295587564914710" style="display:none">OK, I originally gave this 3.5 stars.. but I have decided just to give it 4 stars. <br /><br /><i>“I’m experiencing some teenage angst, Mrs Casnoff,” I answered. “I need to, like, write it in my journal or something.”</i><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />Wow, I read that book in about five hours…. I probably should get some food. Laughter is the only sustenance I need.<br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br /><u>Groundskeepers.</u><br /><br />Sorry, what was the question? <br />Sophie. Jenna. Boarding school. MAGICAL BOARDING SCHOOL FOR DELINQUENT PARANORMALS. Ghosts. Flirtytirty boys. Diversity. Cellar shenanigans. Tattoos. Curses. Bustles. Evil <s>b</s>witches. Ms Hawkins’ deliciously wicked sense of humour. <br /><br /><b>Low Points.</b><br />Yeah, I’m morally opposed to faeries. <br />And characters being jammed into restrictive stereotypes…. LET THEM SOAR.<br /><br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />I loved Sophie and I could really relate to her because <s>I have magical powers</s> , <s>I canoodle with warlocks on a regular basis</s>, she’s such a massive goon. She was so useless and awkward and unaware of herself and goofy and sarcastic and she was such a refreshing narrator because she seemed really… well, real. So many books that I (and my friends!) read are completely saturated with AFPs who are so simpering and vomit-inducing and they get so <i>angry</i> and <i>frustrated</i> because they didn’t ask to be so heart-stoppingly beautiful and have all these boys fall over themselves to be with them. Gaaaaaah. <br />So, when Sophie exploded onto the page with her delinquent paranormal ways, her refreshing humour (a perfect vessel for Ms Hawkins’ gentle ribbing of the genre, no cliché is safe around her!) and boob sweat, it was like taking a breath of fresh air. Although, I wasn’t impressed by her opposition to freckles. What in the world is wrong with freckles?!<br /><br /><i>“So, I have a destiny,” I said. “Crap.”</i><br /><br />Titter.<br />Yes, sometimes Sophie’s sass and smart-arse comments bordered on a bit much… but if she toned that down just a tad, I imagine we’d be best friends forever and sit up all night eating delicious snacks and chortling over her being a witch and having sexy men fawning over her and how it was so cute that I was completely ordinary and stuck with the <i>bad dog</i> in cargo shorts and his excessive slobber.<br />OH, HOW WE WOULD CHORTLE.<br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />Well, in the beginning I could take Archer or leave him. Sure, he was pretty (“<i>So you think I’m pretty?”</i>), and clever and funny and a bit of a wild boy (WILD BOYS….sorry my Duran Duran references are a knee-jerk reaction now… or you could say a Reflex. Ohhh yeah) and he was a massive douche to Sophie but then, wait, he’s actually secretly nice and loves herjsaq9ijecdjksla;sohdfio02eidjfvsn… sorry I just fell asleep.<br />Yeah, he was fine…. He coasted. He was on my radar but he wasn’t making any waves.<br />That was until the end when he suddenly got <i>much more</i> interesting. And ripped, apparently. He’d been keeping <i>that</i> secret under his scruffy blazer and un-tucked shirt, wasn’t he?!<br />And then we have Cal, who isn’t necessarily a love interest in this book but I’m guessing he’s going to lope into the sequel with his plaid shirt and his axe and his rippling pectorals and his inevitable dark and brooding <i>past</i> that Sophie finds mysterious and intriguing.<br />But, yeah… I’ve not worked out how he’ll feature in the sequel yet. It’s got me completely <s>betrothed</s> baffled. <br /><br /><b>Best Friend.</b><br />Lesbian vampire. Um, LOVE IT. Jenna was fantastic and, although Sophie was sometimes a bit unnecessarily cruel to her (Um, wallowing in self-pity?! I’d like to see <i>you</i> try going through what Jenna did, Miss Mercer!), I liked the easy and natural sounding dynamic the two of them had. I have to admit when she came out of the coffin my eyes did begin to roll and my lips began to curl, my natural reaction to vampires. But I needn’t have worried because Jenna was actually a decent vamp and kick-ass unlike so many of her un-dead chums. <br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br />OK, when I first picked up this book I was all smitten and smug (smuggen?) because I had already chosen THE BEST SONG for this book. But then Ms Hawkins with her devious twists and turns (which I will not divulge) completely blew that out of the water. So I thought I was snookered.<br />But then I thought, no. Because I love this song and it is perfect for <s>seducing unsuspecting warlocks in a basement</s> this book…. Until it… well… wasn’t. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vAIAXk0z0lI" rel="nofollow noopener"> Witchy Woman by Eagles</a><br /><br /><b>Angst Level.</b><br />4/10. This book is relatively tame in the angst level. Sure there are a few bits that are borderline grim, but this book is mainly a one-way ticket to FUN TOWN. (That’s right, FUN TOWN) And it was really refreshing to just sit back and take in the view.<br />Although… I gather the sequel is going to be a lot darker.<br />And that’s just fine by me.<br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who want to book a one-way ticket to FUN TOWN. OK, I promise that that’s the last time I’m going to say that… it’s actually making <i>me</i> cringe. People who are looking for a new fictional best friend that will make them realise how boring and ordinary their lives are. People who have always thought their world would end when their acceptance letter to Hogwarts got lost in the post… don’t worry, Hex Hall will take anyone. People who would be able to think of witty responses to a werewolf lunging for your jugular. People who are sick of others being suspicious when they ask them to join their secret coven. People who immediately think of singing Pocahontas songs when they’re outdoors. People who will always lust after the groundskeeper. People who wish their detentions had been <i>that</i> fun… mmmhmmm. People who maintain that boys who are rude/arrogant/downright nasty are just that way because they are completely and secretly besotted with you. It’s true. Right? People who wish their stoopid school had had a prom so they could wear beautiful dresses and get their hair done all fancy… we did get to go to Alton Towers though, which was <i>amazing</i> and didn’t end with a gabiilion girls crying in formal wear, which I imagine happens a lot at proms. Although, I probably would have more luck finding a prom date than finding someone to go on Air for the third time in a row. <i>Wimps</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2771295587564914710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163698323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17246439631012875277">Fun! This book really grew on me. It took several tries to get past the first couple of chapters, but once Sophie finally gets settled in at Hex Hall things start moving along. The witchy battles are pretty cool, there's good build-up of the mystique behind the school and behind Sophie's past and powers, and the author does a nice job with creating a variety of different characters with distinctive voices. I especially liked BFF Jenna and the super cute and witty Archer, and Sophie herself turns</span>
  <span id="freeText17246439631012875277" style="display:none">Fun! This book really grew on me. It took several tries to get past the first couple of chapters, but once Sophie finally gets settled in at Hex Hall things start moving along. The witchy battles are pretty cool, there's good build-up of the mystique behind the school and behind Sophie's past and powers, and the author does a nice job with creating a variety of different characters with distinctive voices. I especially liked BFF Jenna and the super cute and witty Archer, and Sophie herself turns out to be a pretty kick-ass heroine. <br /><br />It did take me a little while to get used to the author's voice, but the humor actually gets to be really good as the story develops and I've gone back to giggle over certain passages again. Overally, this is a really terrific debut and a fast-paced, entertaining read. It's always a plus when a YA author manages to surprise her audience with twists and turns in the plot too, and there are a couple of really good ones here that will leave readers on the edge for more.<br /><br />Besides...you can't not love a girl who tries to stop an attacking werewolf by yelling, "BAD DOG!"</span>

<div id="review_167340787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167340787" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167340787?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167340787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8579043548793222642"><br/>I was so pleasantly surprised by this book, almost as surprised as I am by the fact that I actually decided to read it. I'd all but given up on young adult novels that feature any of the following: vampires, werewolves, witches, shifters, fairies, angels, demons... you get the idea. Young adult fantasy and urban fantasy seems to have been constantly churning out more of the same, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5287473-hex-hall' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hex Hall</a> really ticked all the right boxes for me.<br/><br/>Granted, a boarding school for witches and whatnot isn't exactl</span>
  <span id="freeText8579043548793222642" style="display:none"><br />I was so pleasantly surprised by this book, almost as surprised as I am by the fact that I actually decided to read it. I'd all but given up on young adult novels that feature any of the following: vampires, werewolves, witches, shifters, fairies, angels, demons... you get the idea. Young adult fantasy and urban fantasy seems to have been constantly churning out more of the same, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5287473-hex-hall" rel="nofollow noopener">Hex Hall</a> really ticked all the right boxes for me.<br /><br />Granted, a boarding school for witches and whatnot isn't exactly original and it's a hard field to compete in when you're up against the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K.Rowling</a>, but I liked Hawkins' laid back and kind of chick-lit style writing. The novel reminded me of something in between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> and this TV show that I used to love when I was a kid called 'The Worst Witch', maybe I'm wrong but I'd be willing to bet that not many people outside of the UK have heard of it. Anyway, you basically have all you expect from a regular high school: bullies, bitchiness, crushes, dating, school dances, etc. But then you also have the added trouble that comes with supernatural creatures and magical powers: killers on the loose, demons being summoned, bullies that can turn you into a slug... <br /><br />I won't say that I expected to hate it, but I did expect to be bored. I never imagined there would be moments that made me laugh out loud and annoyingly stereotypical bad boys that are actually hot enough to get away with being annoyingly stereotypical bad boys. Yes, you heard me right: another young adult novel with another hot but dangerous male love interest... but this time I completely loved it. Maybe my mid-life crisis came early but I thought Archer was really hot. If I'd been at Hex Hall I know I would have both hated and wanted to be with him at the same time. I think I liked him most because he had a sense of humour and didn't say really stupid cliched phrases like "I'm wrong for you because I'm so badass" - okay, maybe it doesn't quite go like that but I hate literary heroes that believe they're so bad that they've earned the right to apologise for it. Ugh. My point: Archer wasn't like that.<br /><br />The mystery was alright but it wasn't my favourite bit; the novel's strength was in the characters and the dialogue, not in the plot behind it all. Basically: someone died, someone was accused, real culprit was found out... the end. Probably was what stopped me from giving it 5 stars, my full marks demand a better story. But what the heck, it was fun, I enjoyed it a lot, and I now have every intention of reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7862667-demonglass" rel="nofollow noopener">Demonglass</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8579043548793222642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1258632013" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1258632013?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/21634686-burn">Burn</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1258632013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2549606853781032035"><br/>As to date, this has been one of the most enjoyable fantasy books I’ve read that deals with otherworldly creatures like witches, vampires, faes, werewolves, shape-shifters and demons (collectively called as Prodigium) through the author’s creative effort of putting them all together in one monster high called Hecate Hall or simply Hex Hall. <br/><br/>It’s a fast, fun read told by Sophie, a supposedly powerful witch who at 16 barely knows anything about her real powers. Thus, she gets enrolled at Hex Hall </span>
  <span id="freeText2549606853781032035" style="display:none"><br>As to date, this has been one of the most enjoyable fantasy books I’ve read that deals with otherworldly creatures like witches, vampires, faes, werewolves, shape-shifters and demons (collectively called as Prodigium) through the author’s creative effort of putting them all together in one monster high called Hecate Hall or simply Hex Hall. <br><br>It’s a fast, fun read told by Sophie, a supposedly powerful witch who at 16 barely knows anything about her real powers. Thus, she gets enrolled at Hex Hall which has this Vampire Academy/Hogwart’s vibe but more inclusive.^^<br><br>I could practically imagine <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2261547.Rachel_Hawkins" title="Rachel Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel Hawkins</a> do this in front of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/137902.Richelle_Mead" title="Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Richelle Mead</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K Rowling</a> after writing the book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436331884ra/15447858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Or probably not. Lol! </b><br><br>It’s very enjoyable because the heroine is funny, witty and sarcastic. Exactly my kind of gal! She doesn’t care so much about her appearance. She also knows how to properly appreciate other people’s beauty without a tinge of jealousy.<br><br>The narration and dialogue are delightful and easy to read.<br><br><b> <i> “'I'm experiencing some teenage angst…I need to, like, write in my journal or something." </i></b> <br><br>The events are fast-paced and very interesting. The author manipulated these fantastic characters pretty well and created interesting conflicts and twists although personally, I think the plot could use a bit more action. But this is only the first book of the series, so I’m sure there’ll be a lot of those in the sequel.<br><br><b> This is highly recommended especially for young readers (or even old) looking for a light, enjoyable fantasy read. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2549606853781032035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1276319007" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1276319007?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=your-spesual-is-showing">your-spesual-is-showing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face">protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-should-ve-said-no">i-should-ve-said-no</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1276319007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8779453718367957844"><blockquote>
  <i>"Archer is smart and funny in addition to being hot. Elodie [his girlfriend] is stupid and dull."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442940346ra/16296355.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The second, <i>the second</i>, I read that line, I logged into Goodreads to check which year it was published. <br/><br/>2010. Also known as YA's embarrassing puberty years. I tend to stay away from books published during that time since they're filled with unhealthy romantic relationships and girl-on-girl hate. YA now is like college you, all grown-up and cringing at the occasional photo of your tween self that </span>
  <span id="freeText8779453718367957844" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Archer is smart and funny in addition to being hot. Elodie [his girlfriend] is stupid and dull."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442940346ra/16296355.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The second, <i>the second</i>, I read that line, I logged into Goodreads to check which year it was published. <br><br>2010. Also known as YA's embarrassing puberty years. I tend to stay away from books published during that time since they're filled with unhealthy romantic relationships and girl-on-girl hate. YA now is like college you, all grown-up and cringing at the occasional photo of your tween self that pops up on Facebook.<br><br><b>Hex Hall is juvenile YA.</b> The writing is a more inane version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot" title="Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Meg Cabot</a>'s style, filled with cutesy internal monologues and pop culture references. The plot is an typical mystery type without much punch.<br><br>And the girl hate. <i>God</i>, the girl hate.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I turned and saw Chaston, Anna and Elodie walking toward me. They looked amazing in the fugly gym uniforms. Shocker."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468045443ra/19659544.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unlike Tina Fey's masterpiece, the girls don't make up and sing kumbaya. I thought it was heading that direction for a while and was sadly let down. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Elodie turns out to be a power-hungry bitch after all. Yeah, sure, she passes Sophie her powers in the end. Cry me a river. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>In the acknowledgements, it surprisingly states Hex Hall is mostly about the power of women. <br><br>What power? The power to tear each other down?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Even her essay for Lord Byron's class was about the way physical beauty enhanced a witch's power, supposedly because it gave her easier access to humans. It was ridiculous."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>No, it's <i>smart</i>. Ethics aside, it's a damn good tactic.<br><br>The feminism in Hex Hall reminds me of this movie I watched recently: White Chicks. (I know, it's been out for over a decade, but I wasn't interested until I saw a gif of one of the protagonists telling the other to hold his poodle, so he can beat someone up). It's not devoid of female bonding—Sophie and Jenna's relationship was nicely done—but it relies on knocking down other women to build the home team up. In White Chicks, it's the fake Wilson sisters and their friends against the spoiled heiresses who are willing to sleep their way onto the catwalk. In Hex Hall, it's Sophie and Jenna against the witches' coven who are obsessed with power and their looks.<br><br>I'm sure you're all tired of me banging on about feminism, but it's something I unconsciously look for when I read. I weigh other factors too obviously—plot, pace, characters, the realistic aspect, etc, but gender equality is up there. If a book is awesome enough, I can overlook certain aspects, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a>'s arguably archetypal ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[of a hero needing to rescue his girl. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Hex Hall just fails on all fronts.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8779453718367957844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_155704504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155704504" />
    <a title="chucklesthescot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3426724-chucklesthescot"><img alt="chucklesthescot" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537360628p2/3426724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155704504?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chucklesthescot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chucklesthescot" href="/user/show/3426724-chucklesthescot">chucklesthescot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781847387226" href="/book/show/7791582-hex-hall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer155704504&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155704504" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2384764053714269399">Well this is just the same old tired format for paranormal YA boarding school romps. I've seen the same story time and time again in books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6359599.Secret_Lives__Darke_Academy___1_' title='Secret Lives (Darke Academy, #1) by Gabriella Poole' rel='nofollow noopener'>Secret Lives</a>,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2722413.Evernight__Evernight___1_' title='Evernight (Evernight, #1) by Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evernight</a>,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6611024.Firespell__Dark_Elite___1_' title='Firespell (Dark Elite, #1) by Chloe Neill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Firespell</a>, and it is just boring me.<br/><br/>1)misfit teen sent to boarding school<br/>2)she doesn't want to be there<br/>3)gets on wrong side of popular bitches on day one<br/>4)instant crush on sexiest guy at school<br/>5)her only friend is a fellow misfit<br/>6)grim teachers<br/>7)obnoxious students<br/>8)murderer on the loose<br/><br/>The characters are either obnoxious muppets or</span>
  <span id="freeText2384764053714269399" style="display:none">Well this is just the same old tired format for paranormal YA boarding school romps. I've seen the same story time and time again in books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6359599.Secret_Lives__Darke_Academy___1_" title="Secret Lives (Darke Academy, #1) by Gabriella Poole" rel="nofollow noopener">Secret Lives</a>,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2722413.Evernight__Evernight___1_" title="Evernight (Evernight, #1) by Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Evernight</a>,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6611024.Firespell__Dark_Elite___1_" title="Firespell (Dark Elite, #1) by Chloe Neill" rel="nofollow noopener">Firespell</a>, and it is just boring me.<br /><br />1)misfit teen sent to boarding school<br />2)she doesn't want to be there<br />3)gets on wrong side of popular bitches on day one<br />4)instant crush on sexiest guy at school<br />5)her only friend is a fellow misfit<br />6)grim teachers<br />7)obnoxious students<br />8)murderer on the loose<br /><br />The characters are either obnoxious muppets or cardboard cut-outs that have no depth or interest to them. The teachers don't seem to give a damn about discipline-explain to me why the werewolf who attacked Sophie on her first minute on campus got no punishment? Is attempted murder seen as acceptable at this school? The only one who was given a stern talking to was the guy who saved Sophie by using magic to protect her from the werewolf! Strange moral code from the head teacher don't you think? As usual in these books, the kids do what the hell they like with the teachers ignoring them, which defeats the whole purpose of the school in my opinion. These kids are sent to this school because they can't control their power so surely they should be watched closely!!! I hate stupid plots like this.<br /><br />*sigh* I think it's time to give up on these cloned books and pick up a proper urban fantasy book with a decent story and characters that don't bug me to death.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1581054947502134135">HEX HALL is an insanely fun, hilarious, and HOT book! I can't even tell you how many times I laughed out loud (or had to put the book down because I was laughing so hard)! Sophie Mercer is now officially one of my favorite heroines and I just might be a little bit in love with Archer Cross, too. :) I can't say enough wonderful things about this book, only that you need to pick it up ASAP when it debuts next March. I'm only sad that I have to wait so long to read the next book in the series!!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1258069925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Daiane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32806732-daiane"><img alt="Daiane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457143503p2/32806732.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8568978127780093927"><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>It took me a while to start reading this book. My last Rachel Hawkins one didn't attracted me that much and It's not an original plot. A young witch who screw up and let humans see her magic. Firstly, how can she be that dumb to show her magic to others like nothing? Who she doesn't even know that well and is like "let me be your fairy godmother. Ops, sorry..."<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369282.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Then she is sentenced to a magical boarding school for delinquent supernatural beings...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369283.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And there she makes frien</span>
  <span id="freeText8568978127780093927" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br><br>It took me a while to start reading this book. My last Rachel Hawkins one didn't attracted me that much and It's not an original plot. A young witch who screw up and let humans see her magic. Firstly, how can she be that dumb to show her magic to others like nothing? Who she doesn't even know that well and is like "let me be your fairy godmother. Ops, sorry..."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369282.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then she is sentenced to a magical boarding school for delinquent supernatural beings...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369283.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And there she makes friend with this pinky girly vampire who is her new roommate<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I loved how the homosexual card was played here. Jenna is so sweat and her relationship with Sophie was really awesome. I really liked that we have a book that finally portraits that having a gay girl friend doesn't means she will be different, or that she won't like pink or be feminine or even that she will like you. She is just a sweat friend &lt;3  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><i>
  <b>"This room looked like it had been decorated by the unholy lovechild of Barbie and Strawberry Shortcake.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019283ra/17369288.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And falls for the hot guy who is the mean queen bee's boyfriend, who btw, has some Draco Malfoy vibe.<br><br><i>
  <b>“It’s Archer Cross, and I’m the first one. Now what about you?” He squinted. “Let’s see . . . brown hair, freckles, whole girl-next-door vibe going on . . . Allie? Lacie? Definitely something cutesy ending in ie.”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369284.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, The first half of the book was really tiring. Sophie is too slow and sometimes she was too dumb. Although I kinda liked when she was really useless as a witch because, well, we are useless.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I wish I could say that I suddenly discovered my inner warrior princess and expertly leaped at Archer, weapon hoisted high, teeth bared. That would have been cool.<br>Instead I raised the stake to about shoulder height and took two, maybe three shuffling steps forward.<br>Then viselike fingers clenched my throat, the stake was wrenched from my hand, and a sharp stabbing pain shot up my right thigh as I landed on the ground with a thump that knocked the breath out of me.”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438130432ra/15667840.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> However, It was full of unnecessary parts and some characters were not well explored. There were people (or monsters) that were really well introduced and they never appeared again. Or were just a cameo in the corner of the story. I also expected more from the professors. Not a Minerva McGonagall kind of development, but something. There were also things told over and over again, like the reader didn't get it the first time. And the second. And the third...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369285.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, as all normal schools, at Hecate there were also evil bitches, I mean, witches. Sophie is called to the "coven" but... You know. We also get the hate-love plot as a bonus and things happens...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450019221ra/17369286.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And FINALLY, at the end of second half, the book starts for me. Archer is still far away from my head. He still bothers me and how he was described, with all his hotness... I don't know, it was just too lame. I'm actually more interested in Cal...<br>And we get action!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436060680ra/15414192.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the plot twist, even though it's not THAT good, it's still really interesting. I wasn't expecting the end and all the mystery got me by surprise. That really increased my ratings. So yes, I recommend this book but be aware of the laziness in the beginning and all the teen feelings.<br><br><i>
  <b>"Sorry, sorry. I'l try to stop with the pop culture references."</b>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038953860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2298561404179263194">This book was pretty good. There was action, suspense, and some romance. The main character was witty and any reader would be able to relate to them since she had boy, friend, family and identity problems. This book occasionally reminded me of Harry Potter because of some of the teachers being both harsh and grandmotherly at times. Rachel Hawkins also captured the rea high school life and drama in this with their own version of Prom, cliques, relationships, and talking about teachers behind thei</span>
  <span id="freeText2298561404179263194" style="display:none">This book was pretty good. There was action, suspense, and some romance. The main character was witty and any reader would be able to relate to them since she had boy, friend, family and identity problems. This book occasionally reminded me of Harry Potter because of some of the teachers being both harsh and grandmotherly at times. Rachel Hawkins also captured the rea high school life and drama in this with their own version of Prom, cliques, relationships, and talking about teachers behind their backs. The ending was sad somewhat but you are going to have to read to find out what it is :) Overall this book is good if you are looking for:<br />a good introduction to a series<br />suspense<br />fantasy<br />romance<br />and great characters.</span>

<div id="review_170392416" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170392416" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307662921p2/3813315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170392416?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy">Lucy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=gloomy">gloomy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=better-than-i-expected">better-than-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170392416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12133585489808395305">My main impression from the book is that it's meant for the very bottom of the age spectrum it's being marketed for. I'd say 10-14 years old because the writing is extremely simplistic. Of course, there's a lot of dead teenagers flying around so it's a weird mix of older, more mature themes and fairly immature writing. The world building is so-so. There wasn't a lot of depth here despite being charming in a general kind of way. Female Harry Potter, Sophie Mercer is not, but still fanatic Potter </span>
  <span id="freeText12133585489808395305" style="display:none">My main impression from the book is that it's meant for the very bottom of the age spectrum it's being marketed for. I'd say 10-14 years old because the writing is extremely simplistic. Of course, there's a lot of dead teenagers flying around so it's a weird mix of older, more mature themes and fairly immature writing. The world building is so-so. There wasn't a lot of depth here despite being charming in a general kind of way. Female Harry Potter, Sophie Mercer is not, but still fanatic Potter fans might find something here.<br /><br />The book moves at a brisk pace and Sophie, the female lead, is adorable and funny. The book tosses a lot of cliches in a blender and while you're perfectly aware you're being served every paranormal plot device ever it still goes down smoothly enough. I wouldn't recommend it to adults who like reading the genre. I'm giving my copy to the teenage girl who lives next door.</span>

  <span id="freeText608380927819915821" style="display:none">Welcome to Monster College! I mean Hecate Academy <br> <br>I’m sorry but how is this book not more wellknow haha (ಥ ̯ ಥ). It has all the elements!<br><br>We got juvenile <b>delinquent SUPERNATURALS</b>, heroine coming into her powers, <b>secret society</b> trying to kill all supes, and a murdering spree at the monster college! <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442790311ra/16278415.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556817836ra/27446149.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So allow me to set the scene: <br><br><b>Sophie Mercer</b>, witch delinquent extraordinaire <br><br>I love Sophie’s attitude and snarkiness. There’s something about this character that just makes you grip the pages and keep reading until it’s done. <b>She is fierce, loyal, brave</b> and one of the most goddamn sarcastic and wittiest characters I have ever read. <br><br><b>
  <i>“I should say upfront that I have never been in a cellar in my life. In fact, I can see no reason why anyone should ever go into a cellar unless there is wine involved.”</i>
</b><br><br>She’s new to the school so naturally she makes friends and enemies within the first… 3 days there ?? <br><br>We got a GAY vampire BFF named <b>Jenna</b> and she is the ONLY acceptable <i>*SPARKLY VAMPIRE*</i> in my opinion ! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243631.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I friggenn loved their friendship, it was finally friends who each had their own fully realized characters and stories *and finally legit LGBT+ represent, and not just tokenized* <br><br>Plus they were funny as fuck when they were together trying to survive school and learning their powers <br><br><b>The world building</b> not only was the general premise of the world to help train troubled teen supes was just bloody brilliant. <br><br>But I also just love how this book didn’t take itself seriously. <b>It took all the funny school cliches and worked it into the supernatural theme</b> that just made the book all the more fun to read. For example we got <br><br>The witchy mean girls <b>Anna, Chaston and Elodie </b><br><br><b>
  <i>“I wondered if they had rehearsed this weird three-way-talking thing they had going on. <br>I imagined them sitting in a circle in their dorm room, brushing their hair and saying, "Okay, so I'll say we feel bad, and then you'll say that your hot boyfriend thinks she's pathetic.” </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509907709ra/24369839.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fucking iconicc<br><br>And <br><b>Archer</b>, typical hot bad boy in YA novels. He a powerful wizard who sorta totally abuses his power and sasses the fuck outta everyone <br><br><b>
  <i>”You know," someone said off to my left, "I usually find a blocking spell to be a lot more effective than yelling 'Bad dog,' but maybe that's just me."<br><br>I turned. Leaning against a tree, his collar unbuttoned and tie loose, was a smirking guy. His Hecate blazer was hanging limply in the crook of his elbow.<br><br>"You are a witch, aren't you?" he continued, “Maybe in the future, you could endeavor not to suck so badly at it.” </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601251091ra/30161818.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay ya’ll know that YA is definitely not my style to say in the least…. <br><br>But this was the first series I ever read that first sparked my love and interest of books…. To me, this was my first Kate Daniels type hype book<br><br>Each of these characters are DEVELOPED with their own stories, motives, backstories and fucking dope ass abilities. <br><br>A quick, easy read with lots of intense action and witty one-liners. I love how this school is for all the shitty supes that are trying to figure out their powers while surviving school, AND theres a murderer running around or some shit <br><br>So being YA, ya gotta be in right mind slash age to really enjoy it otherwise it could lose those same levels of *spicy* and surprise, Sophie and this world will always have a special place to me <br><br><b>
  <i>“She plunged her snout into my hair and took a deep shuddering breath.<br>A warm string of drool dripped from her open maw onto my bare shoulder.<br>I forced myself to stay very calm, and after a moment, she released me.<br>Giving a bashful shrug, she said, "Sorry. Werewolf thing."<br>"Hey, no problem," I said, even though all I could think was, Slobber! Werewolf slobber! On my skin!”</i>

<div id="review_1193867952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1193867952" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10697179-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549097p2/10697179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1193867952?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/10697179-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1193867952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11057753777008945804">I am possibly one of the only people who hasn't read Rebel Belle so I didn't know how amazing Rachel Hawkins was at writing! There is nothing extremely spectacular about her writing there aren't really intricate profound quotes and there aren't any special qualities that set her apart like poetry prose or anything of the sort, but all of that is why her writing is so great. She took a very plain storyline, something done before, and made it incredibly unique and beautiful because it was so real.</span>
  <span id="freeText11057753777008945804" style="display:none">I am possibly one of the only people who hasn't read Rebel Belle so I didn't know how amazing Rachel Hawkins was at writing! There is nothing extremely spectacular about her writing there aren't really intricate profound quotes and there aren't any special qualities that set her apart like poetry prose or anything of the sort, but all of that is why her writing is so great. She took a very plain storyline, something done before, and made it incredibly unique and beautiful because it was so real. <br />For instance, her characters were so perfect. Sophie was everything you would expect her to be given her situation. She was a giving caring character who was also definitely selfish and she second guessed herself and others all the time, all the while giving chances to the underdog. She is in reality a well rounded character that I could see existing in the world and that's so rare.<br />Besides the supernatural beings, this was a very realistic book. They go to classes, they sometimes suck at classes, she got detention, there was a cute boy with a girlfriend who happened to be the mean girl. It was basically the supernatural version of mean girls if they had been at a boarding school and I loved it. <br />So simple. This is not a book that you spend 100 days trying to get over, this isn't a book that you can't stop thinking about, but it's a really good fun book to immerse yourself in for a few hours. Really enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11057753777008945804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2648386780?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11193238-hex-hall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2648386780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14631126471287499928">Ok. It’s time I admitted to myself that I have a penchant for fantasy set in a school setting. I’m too old for this to be the case but unfortunately my heart and mind don’t care! My first outing with this author and she definitely has similarities to Maureen Johnson books, which I also love. So in this world we have prodigious who are witches, fae, vampires, ruled by a council. Also demons. There’s a love interest and bullying and a feisty funny heroine. Very enjoyable read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br><br>All in all this wasn’t a <i>terrible</i> book, but I’m not a fan of book series in general and I’m <b>really</b> not a fan of reading 323 pages where 200+ probably could have been cut and combined with book #2. I continue to cross my fingers in hopes this trend will pass and authors will only be signed to produce one book at a time. Hopefully the result will be books that aren't always soooooooo open ended.<br><br>Off topic: In my quest to hunt down what seems to be every witch-related picture/gif on the interwebs, I discovered a couple of things. <div id="review_589849692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/589849692" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/589849692?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589849692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9635268582397543215">Via Book Reviews by Niki Hawkes at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.nikihawkes.com'>www.nikihawkes.com</a><br/><br/><br/>This is one of those books that I’m kicking myself for not reading sooner. One of my best go-to girls for books recommended it to me like three years ago when it first came out, but it wasn’t until I got an arc of Hawkins’ latest, School Spirits, that I finally got motivated enough to pick it up. Stupid. I loved it! It was fun without being cheesy, dark without being depressing, and all-around a delightful book.<br/><br/>Here’s another reason why I’m ki</span>
  <span id="freeText9635268582397543215" style="display:none">Via Book Reviews by Niki Hawkes at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nikihawkes.com">www.nikihawkes.com</a><br /><br /><br />This is one of those books that I’m kicking myself for not reading sooner. One of my best go-to girls for books recommended it to me like three years ago when it first came out, but it wasn’t until I got an arc of Hawkins’ latest, School Spirits, that I finally got motivated enough to pick it up. Stupid. I loved it! It was fun without being cheesy, dark without being depressing, and all-around a delightful book.<br /><br />Here’s another reason why I’m kicking myself: I love books that take place at schools. Give me a school for anything, basket-weaving, sword-fighting, dog-sledding – you name it. If it takes place at a school I want to read it. What I liked about this Academy in particular was how much of an impact it had on the story. Everything from the location of the school to how the students felt inside it transformed Hex Hall from a setting into a character. Hawkins used a lot of great imagery when describing it setting the mood for the entire book.<br /><br />The overall “feel” for the book is probably my favorite part. While the school had a tremendous impact on that, it wouldn’t have been near as memorable without such a lovable protagonist. Not only is she fluent in sarcasm but she also maintains a quiet strength in the things that make her different from everybody else. And she was funny – I cracked up several times throughout the book. What’s more, I enjoyed all of the side characters just as much… particularly the love interest. <br /><br />Overall, this book delivered a memorable setting, great protagonist, a fun mystery, paranormal creatures, and a compelling love story. It blew my expectations away and has quickly become one of the best books I’ve read this year.<br /><br />Recommendations: if Vampire Academy and Bloodlines are on your favorites list, you should definitely give this book try. It’s perfect for those who like paranormal and want a fun and memorable mystery/love story. If it’s already in your TBR pile, pick it up now – you won’t be sorry!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9635268582397543215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158709795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11056604411123861230">I would like to thank Ate<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1258632013' rel='nofollow noopener'> AJ</a> and Ate <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332608939' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel</a> for recommending this book to me. (Click their names to read their reviews) This paranormal fantasy novel is <b>fun, quick and entertaining </b> to read. I've listened to the audio book and is narrated by Cris Dukehart (she's really good by the way). <br/><br/>When a spell gone bad, a young witch Sophie Mercer was sent to Hecate Hall (Hex Hall) as a punishment of exposing herself to humans. Students consists of young Prodigium or supernatural creatures like vampires, w</span>
  <span id="freeText11056604411123861230" style="display:none">I would like to thank Ate<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1258632013" rel="nofollow noopener"> AJ</a> and Ate <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332608939" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel</a> for recommending this book to me. (Click their names to read their reviews) This paranormal fantasy novel is <b>fun, quick and entertaining </b> to read. I've listened to the audio book and is narrated by Cris Dukehart (she's really good by the way). <br /><br />When a spell gone bad, a young witch Sophie Mercer was sent to Hecate Hall (Hex Hall) as a punishment of exposing herself to humans. Students consists of young Prodigium or supernatural creatures like vampires, werewolves, fairies, witches etc. Things happened when there are mysterious attacks towards the students and they think Jenna (Sophie's vampire roommate) is responsible for these attacks. Sophie doesn't believe in it and she's about to find out.<br /> <br />The setting somewhat reminds me of <i>Harry Potter</i> and the Hex Hall's history made me curious. It's pretty interesting and I want to know more. <b>Sophie Mercer is such a fascinating character.</b> She's witty, hilarious and sarcastic at its best. This lady made me laugh out loud. As for other characters, all of them are interesting. Especially Archer Cross. Oh how I love this bad boy warlock. Lastly, the plot twist in this book is something I didn't expect. I was like "WHOA! Now, that <i>is</i> one good twist!" What a great surprise.<br /><br />Overall, I really like this book. I am definitely going to pick up the sequel. If you are looking for a light fantasy novel, give this one a try. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11056604411123861230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/428202845?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8416819-hex-hall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=at-my-library">at-my-library</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428202845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5295437713684774626">**3.5 stars**<br/> <br/>When my husband asked me what I was reading today, I summed this book up to him as, "Harry Potter chick lit". I meant that as a complement. "Hex Hall" is a really adorable and spunky YA paranormal read. It is what <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9439989.Touch_of_Frost__Mythos_Academy___1_' title='Touch of Frost (Mythos Academy, #1) by Jennifer Estep' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mythos Academy</a> tried to be before it fell miserably short. I was shocked at how much fun I had reading this book. <br/><br/>The most successful parts of this story were the characters and the witty dialogue. Sophie was an awesome MC. She was funny (I surprised myself by laughing ou</span>
  <span id="freeText5295437713684774626" style="display:none">**3.5 stars**<br /> <br />When my husband asked me what I was reading today, I summed this book up to him as, "Harry Potter chick lit". I meant that as a complement. "Hex Hall" is a really adorable and spunky YA paranormal read. It is what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9439989.Touch_of_Frost__Mythos_Academy___1_" title="Touch of Frost (Mythos Academy, #1) by Jennifer Estep" rel="nofollow noopener">Mythos Academy</a> tried to be before it fell miserably short. I was shocked at how much fun I had reading this book. <br /><br />The most successful parts of this story were the characters and the witty dialogue. Sophie was an awesome MC. She was funny (I surprised myself by laughing out loud at some of the phrases Sophie dishes out), accepting, and not clichéd (bonus points for that one!). I found her to be totally relatable and believable. <br /><br />A typical Sophie line:<br /><i>I opened my eyes to stare at a bright blue tulle monstrosity with a skirt that would hit me at mid thigh. I'd look like the really slutty bride of Cookie Monster.</i><br /><br />The secondary characters were also pretty great. How could I not love a lesbian friend in a mainstream YA novel... I can't, I must love her. Three cheers for diversity! And Archer is <i>such</i> an adorable boy to crush on (even if that makes me a touch pervy). <br /><br />What kept this book from being a <i>great</i> read was that it was a bit too slow for my tastes. It wasn't spooky enough, or dangerous enough... it just wasn't enough for me. The pace dragged at the beginning and the excitement came too little too late for my tastes. However, I'm excited that I have another YA paranormal to get behind!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5295437713684774626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's iconic...)</i><br/><br/><br/>This was one of the first books that I added to my TBR pile, right after taking recommendations from Booktube and I was really excited to start reading it (even tho I had postpone for years.... ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ ).<br/>It isn't really what I had expect but that doesn't mean that I enjoyed it any less, just that the hype for this book was too high.<br/><br/>When I finally got a chance to pick it up, it took me only a few hours to finish the entire book in one sitting.<br/>It is really fast </span>
  <span id="freeText1781249013336620517" style="display:none"><b><i>"BAD DOG!"</i></b> <br> <i>(What? It's iconic...)</i><br><br><br>This was one of the first books that I added to my TBR pile, right after taking recommendations from Booktube and I was really excited to start reading it (even tho I had postpone for years.... ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ ).<br>It isn't really what I had expect but that doesn't mean that I enjoyed it any less, just that the hype for this book was too high.<br><br>When I finally got a chance to pick it up, it took me only a few hours to finish the entire book in one sitting.<br>It is really fast paced and lightly written. Our protagonist is quite funny and the story is very interessting but I honestly have to say that this was the most anticlimactic "battle" I have ever come across, nothing didn't really happened. <b>Literally nothing.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493682546ra/22641908.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote>Sophie is a teenage witch who struggles to keep her powers hidden, which makes her and her mother move alot. She has never met her father. The only thing she knows about him is that her powers came from his side of the family and that when her mother found out he was a Warlock, she dumped him and left without knowing that she was pregnant. When Sophie was born she thought it would be better if he wasn't involve in her life, so everything that Sophie knows about her powers are the things that her mom read about in houndreds of magic books and from discovering some thing by herself.<br>This did seem to work until one day she went to far and was forced to enroll into Hex Hall, an academy for supernatural missfits. There she finds her first best friend, 3 enemys and big crush on a guy she shouldn't crush on and all that on her first day there.<br>But when her best friend get's acused on the murder on her former roomate and other 2 attacks, Sophie tries to find out who was really behind them, while struggeling with her powers and discovering that she maybe plays a bigger part in all this then she realized.<br>In the end she has to ask herself, where come her powers from and why is her lif in danger? Who can she really trust when friends and foes look so much alike...</blockquote></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('16FcKFuTmtZij0+RwEJk7+JlfKtNZahEXr+ZGbRCGjrCNkFANHI9RjSPk6F7BWlh8WIFkb8W2RWoR1MZZBSLkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cypm4csj5euz0k1yYCMVIoun4BxCktLks1BoyT+xyu9mvXuJpMJCe+XSkULbZBismKCZJrDho7VFqKLJ7+dbRQ==')})
  }
